<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our ability to achieve identical supermarket
sales and earnings growth and earnings per share goals may be affected by:
labor disputes, particularly as the Company seeks to manage health care and
pension costs; industry consolidation; pricing and promotional activities of
existing and new competitors, including non-traditional competitors and the
aggressiveness of that competition; our response to these actions; unexpected
changes in product costs; the state of the economy, including interest rates
and the inflationary and deflationary trends in certain commodities; the extent
to which our customers exercise caution in their purchasing behavior in
response to economic conditions; the number of shares outstanding; the success
of our future growth plans; goodwill impairment; volatility in our fuel
margins, which will be affected by changes in fuel costs; and our ability to
generate sales at desirable margins, as well as the success of our programs
designed to increase our identical sales without fuel. In addition, any delays
in opening new stores, or changes in the economic climate could cause us to
fall short of our sales and earnings targets.&#160;
Our ability to increase identical supermarket sales also could be
adversely affected by increased competition and sales shifts to other stores
that we operate, as well as increases in sales of our corporate brand products.
Earnings and sales also may be affected by adverse weather conditions,
particularly to the extent that hurricanes, tornadoes, floods, and other
conditions disrupt our operations or those of our suppliers; create shortages
in the availability or increases in the cost of products that we sell in our
stores or materials and ingredients we use in our manufacturing facilities; or
raise the cost of supplying energy to our various operations.&nbsp;Our results
also will be affected by the inconsistent pace of the economic recovery,
changes in government-funded benefit programs, consumer confidence, and changes
in inflation and deflation in product and operating costs. Our guidance for
LIFO is based on our forecast of cost changes for products in our inventory.
Our estimate of product cost changes could be affected by general economic
conditions, weather, availability of raw materials and ingredients in the
products that we sell and their packaging, and other factors beyond our
control. Our non-fuel operating margin guidance could change if we are unable
to pass on any cost increases, if our strategies fail to deliver the cost savings
contemplated, or if changes in the cost of our inventory and the timing of
those changes differ from our expectations.&#160;
Our LIFO charge and the timing of our recognition of LIFO expense will
be affected by changes in product costs during the year.&nbsp; Our fuel margins
could fail to average 12&#162; per gallon if rapid changes in fuel costs
occur.&nbsp; Our capital expenditures, and the number of projects that we
complete, could vary from our expectations if we are unsuccessful in acquiring
suitable sites for new stores; development costs vary from those budgeted; our
logistics and technology or store projects are not completed on budget or
within the time frame projected; or if current operating conditions fail to
improve, or worsen.&#160; Square footage
growth during the year is dependent upon our ability to acquire desirable sites
for construction of new facilities, as well as the timing of completion of
projects.&#160; Any change in tax laws,</font></p>

</head>

<body lang="EN-US">

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="right" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:right;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Exhibit&nbsp;99.1</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">KROGER REPORTS THIRD QUARTER 2010 RESULTS</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Net Earnings Increased,&nbsp;Identical
Supermarket Sales Up 2.4% Without Fuel</font></i></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">CINCINNATI,
Ohio, December&nbsp;2, 2010 &#151; The Kroger Co. (NYSE: KR) today reported total
sales, which include fuel, increased 5.9% to $18.7 billion in the third quarter
of fiscal 2010 compared with $17.7 billion for the same period last year.&#160; Excluding fuel sales, total sales increased
3.1% in the third quarter, which ended November&nbsp;6, 2010, over the same
period last year.&#160; Identical supermarket
sales, without fuel, increased 2.4% in the third quarter over the same period
last year.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net earnings for the third quarter of fiscal 2010
totaled $202.2 million, or $0.32 per diluted share.&#160; In the third quarter of fiscal 2009, Kroger
reported a net loss of $874.9 million, or $1.35 per diluted share.&#160; The fiscal 2009 results included non-cash
asset impairment charges totaling $1.05 billion, after tax, that primarily
resulted from a goodwill write-down.&#160;
Excluding these impairment charges, net earnings for the quarter would
have been $176.7 million, or $0.27 per diluted share (Table 6).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;Kroger&#146;s customers today are looking for lower
prices and a great shopping experience, and our Customer 1</font><font size="1" style="font-size:6.5pt;position:relative;top:-3.0pt;">st</font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#160;strategy delivers all that and
more,&#148; said David B. Dillon, Kroger&#146;s chairman and chief executive
officer.&#160; &#147;Our team increased identical
supermarket sales, earnings and earnings per share in the third quarter while
controlling expenses to keep prices low for our customers.&#160; These results show Kroger&#146;s strategy is
working and that our core grocery business is strong and resilient.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Details of Third Quarter 2010 Results</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Including Kroger&#146;s retail fuel operations, FIFO
gross margin (Table 1) was 22.14% of sales for the third quarter of fiscal
2010, a decrease of 56 basis points compared to the third quarter last
year.&#160; Excluding retail fuel operations,
FIFO gross margin decreased 10 basis points.&#160;
Supermarket selling gross margin (Table 1) declined 13 basis points
without fuel.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='',FILE='C:\JMS\bvanga\10-22301-1\task4381179\22301-1-mm-01.htm',USER='bvanga',CD='Dec  2 07:20 2010' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Including Kroger&#146;s retail fuel operations,
operating, general and administrative (OG&amp;A) costs were 17.11% of sales, a
decline of 65 basis points compared with the third quarter last year.&#160; Excluding retail fuel operations and adjusting
for the impairment charges in fiscal 2009, OG&amp;A decreased 14 basis points
from the same period last year.&#160; Positive
identical sales growth, good cost control, and productivity improvements offset
the continued challenge of rising credit card fees, health care and pension
costs.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kroger&#146;s operating margin increased 6 basis points
as a percentage of sales from the same period last year, excluding retail fuel
operations and adjusting for the impairment charges in fiscal 2009.&#160; Including retail fuel operations and the
impairment charges in fiscal 2009, Kroger&#146;s operating margin increased 647
basis points as a percentage of sales compared to the same period last
year.&#160; The impairment charges in fiscal
2009 accounted for 643 basis points of the increase.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Financial Strategy</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Capital investment, excluding acquisitions and
purchases of leased facilities, totaled $484.0 million for the third quarter,
compared with $552.1 million for the same period last year.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At the end of the third quarter, net total debt
(Table 5) was $7.2 billion, a decrease of $489.3 million from a year ago.&#160; On a rolling four-quarters basis, Kroger&#146;s
net total debt to EBITDA ratio was 1.93, which is consistent with the same
period last year after adjusting for the impairment charges in fiscal 2009.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the third quarter, Kroger invested $64.0
million to repurchase 2.9 million shares of stock at an average price of $21.72
per share.&#160; At the end of the quarter,
approximately $352.5 million remained under the $500 million stock repurchase
program announced in June&nbsp;2010.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Fiscal 2010 Year-to-Date Results</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the first three quarters of fiscal 2010, total
sales were $62.3 billion compared with $58.2 billion for the same period last
year.&#160; Excluding fuel sales, total sales
increased 3.2% over the prior year.&#160; For
the same period, identical supermarket sales, excluding fuel, increased 2.5%.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='',FILE='C:\JMS\bvanga\10-22301-1\task4381179\22301-1-mm-01.htm',USER='bvanga',CD='Dec  2 07:20 2010' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net earnings for the first three quarters of fiscal
2010 were $837.5 million, or $1.30 per diluted share.&#160; Kroger reported a net loss of $185.4 million
for the first three quarters of fiscal 2009, or $0.29 per diluted share.&#160; Excluding the impairment charges, net
earnings would have been $866.2 million, or $1.33 per diluted share (Table 6)
for the first three quarters of last year.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kroger&#146;s operating margin for the first three
quarters of fiscal 2010 decreased 38 basis points as a percentage of sales from
the same period last year, excluding retail fuel operations and adjusting for
the impairment charges in fiscal 2009.&#160;
Including retail fuel operations and the impairment charges in fiscal
2009, Kroger&#146;s operating margin increased 160 basis points as a percentage of
sales compared to the same period last year.&#160;
The impairment charges in fiscal 2009 accounted for 195 basis points of
the increase.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Fiscal
2010 Annual Guidance</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kroger narrowed its annual identical supermarket
sales guidance for fiscal 2010.&#160; The
Company now expects identical supermarket sales growth, excluding fuel, to
range between 2.5% and 3.0%.&#160; The
previous guidance range was 2.0% to 3.0%.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For full-year net earnings, Kroger narrowed its
guidance range to $1.65 to $1.78 per diluted share.&#160; The Company is striving to achieve results in
the upper half of this guidance range.&#160;
The previous range was $1.60 to $1.80 per diluted share.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kroger now expects to invest approximately $1.8 to
$2.0 billion in capital projects during the fiscal year.&#160; This compares to earlier guidance of $1.9 to
$2.1 billion.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;Our enthusiastic Kroger team shines during the
holiday season, and we expect a solid end to our fiscal year,&#148; Mr.&nbsp;Dillon
said.&nbsp; &#147;We remain focused on delivering sustainable earnings growth today
for our shareholders while investing for the future.&#160; In addition, Kroger&#146;s stock buyback program,
debt reduction, and recent dividend increase in September&nbsp;demonstrate our
ongoing commitment to creating value.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kroger,
the nation&#146;s largest traditional grocery retailer, employs more than 334,000
associates who serve customers in 2,461 supermarkets and multi-department
stores in 31 states under two dozen local banner names including Kroger, City
Market, Dillons, Jay C, </font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Food
4 Less, Fred Meyer, Fry&#146;s, King Soopers, QFC, Ralphs and Smith&#146;s.&#160; The Company also operates 784 convenience
stores, 375 fine jewelry stores, 954 supermarket fuel centers and 40 food
processing plants in the U.S.&#160; Kroger,
headquartered in Cincinnati, Ohio, focuses its charitable efforts on supporting
hunger relief, health and wellness initiatives, and local organizations in the
communities it serves.&#160; For more
information about Kroger, please visit www.kroger.com.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"># # #</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note:&#160; Fuel sales have historically had low FIFO
gross margin and OG&amp;A rates as compared to corresponding rates on non-fuel
sales.&#160; Additionally, pricing and margins
in Kroger&#146;s retail fuel operations can be volatile on a quarterly basis.&#160; As a result, Kroger discloses such rates,
both including and excluding the effect of retail fuel operations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This
press release contains certain forward-looking statements about the future
performance of the Company.&nbsp; These statements are based on management&#146;s
assumptions and beliefs in light of the information currently available to
it.&nbsp; Such statements are indicated by words such as &#147;guidance&#148; and &#147;expects.&#148;&nbsp;
Aggressive competition, economic conditions, interest rates, goodwill
impairment, the success of programs designed to increase our identical
supermarket sales without fuel, and labor disputes, particularly as the Company
seeks to manage increases in health care and pension costs, could materially
affect our expected identical supermarket sales growth and earnings per share.
Earnings per share also will be affected by the number of shares outstanding,
as well as the volatility in the Company&#146;s fuel margins, which will be affected
by changes in fuel costs.&nbsp; Earnings and sales also may be affected by
adverse weather conditions, particularly to the extent that hurricanes,
tornadoes, floods, and other conditions disrupt our operations or those of our
suppliers; create shortages in the availability or increases in the cost of
products that we sell in our stores or materials and ingredients we use in our
manufacturing facilities; or raise the cost of supplying energy to our various
operations.&nbsp; Our results also will be affected by rising commodity costs,
the inconsistency of the economic recovery, changes in government-funded benefit
programs, consumer confidence, and changes in inflation and deflation in
product and operating costs.&nbsp; Our capital expenditures could vary from our
expectations if we are unsuccessful in acquiring suitable sites for new stores;
development costs vary from those budgeted; our logistics and technology or
store projects are not completed on budget or within the time frame projected;
or if current operating conditions fail to improve, or worsen.&nbsp; These
forward-looking statements are subject to uncertainties and other factors that
could cause actual results to differ materially.&nbsp; We assume no obligation
to update the information contained herein.&nbsp; Please refer to Kroger&#146;s
reports and filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission for a further
discussion of these risks and uncertainties.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note:&#160;
Kroger&#146;s quarterly conference call with investors will be broadcast live
online at 10&nbsp;a.m. (ET) on December&nbsp;2, 2010 at www.kroger.com and
www.streetevents.com.&#160; An on-demand </font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note:
Certain prior-year amounts have been reclassified to conform to current-year
presentation.&#160; Certain per share amounts
and percentages may not sum due to rounding.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note:&#160; The Company defines FIFO gross margin, as
described in the earnings release, as sales minus merchandise costs, including
advertising, warehousing and transportation, but excluding the Last-In
First-Out (LIFO) charge.&#160; This measure is
included to reflect trends in current cost of product.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note:&#160; The Company defines selling gross margin, as
described in the earnings release related to the Company&#146;s supermarkets, as
gross margin before incurring expenses directly related to distributing and merchandising
the products on its store shelves.&#160; These
expenses include advertising, warehousing, transportation, and shrink.&#160; Selling gross margin is a measure of how
competitively the Company is pricing the products it sells.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Merchandise costs and operating, general and
administrative expenses exclude depreciation and amortization expense and rent
expense which are included in separate expense lines.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">LIFO charges of $11.5 and $9.9 were recorded in the
third quarter of 2010 and 2009, respectively.&#160;
For the year-to-date period, LIFO charges of $38.5 and $47.7 were
recorded for 2010 and 2009, respectively.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

important to review them in conjunction with Kroger&#146;s financial results
reported in accordance with GAAP.&#160; Other

differently than Kroger does, limiting the comparability of these measures.</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 27.0pt;text-indent:-27.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kroger defines a supermarket
as identical when it has been open without expansion or relocation for five
full quarters.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 27.0pt;text-indent:-27.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kroger defines a supermarket
as comparable when it has been open for five full quarters, including
expansions and relocations.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Table 5.&#160;
Reconciliation of Total Debt to Net Total Debt</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(in millions)</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(unaudited)</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net
total debt should not be considered an alternative to any GAAP measure of
performance or liquidity.&#160; Management
believes net total debt is an important measure of liquidity, and a primary
component of measuring compliance with the financial covenants under the
Company&#146;s credit facility.&#160; Net total
debt should be reviewed in conjunction with Kroger&#146;s financial results reported
in accordance with GAAP.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
following table provides a reconciliation of total debt to net total debt and
compares the balance in the third quarter of 2010 to the balance in the third
quarter of 2009.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Table 6. Net Earnings Per Diluted Share Excluding
Impairment Charges</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(in millions, except per share amounts)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Items
identified in this table should not be considered alternatives to net earnings
(loss) attributable to The Kroger Co. or any other GAAP measure of
performance.&#160; These items should not be
reviewed in isolation or considered substitutes of the Company&#146;s financial
results as reported in accordance with GAAP.&#160;
Due to the nature of these items, as further described below in the
footnotes, it is important to identify these items and to review them in
conjunction with the Company&#146;s financial results reported in accordance with
GAAP.</font></p>

include charges that were recorded as components of asset impairment charge and
goodwill impairment charge.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">After-tax
goodwill impairment charge ($1,112.7 pre-tax) relating to a Southern California
reporting unit.&#160; Most of the goodwill
impairment charge is non-deductible for tax purposes.</font></p>

impairment charges ($24.1 pre-tax) relating to underperforming stores in a
Southern California reporting unit.</font></p>
